The Cause-Based Definition of a Definer
Author presents cause-based definition with examples and condition of predication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the cause-based definition of a definer to test whether a given term is a valid definer, and explain why mutual correlatives are excluded.

Core Idea
A definer's knowledge causes knowledge of the defined only when predicated on it.

Some logicians replaced 'implication' with 'cause' in defining what a definer is. This shift refines the condition: the definer's conception must be a cause for knowing the defined, but only when predicated on the defined. This excludes mutual correlatives and clarifies the function of definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Extract the cause-based definition
Find in the Arabic the definition: 'the definer of a thing is that whose knowledge is a cause for knowledge of that thing when it is predicated upon it.' Understand that 'knowledge' here means conception (tasawwur).
The key phrase: ما تكون معرفته سببا لمعرفة ذلك الشيء عند حمله عليه
2
Identify what it excludes
The definition excludes mutual correlatives (al-mutadāyifān), since neither's conception is a cause for the other. For example, 'father' and 'son' are known together, not one as cause of the other.
This matches the earlier exclusion using 'implication'.
3
Analyze the examples
Two examples are given: 'rational animal' for complete definition (hadd tāmm) and 'the one who laughs' for incomplete definition (rasm). Note that 'rational animal' when predicated on 'man' causes conception of man's essence; 'the one who laughs' distinguishes man from others.
The definer must be predicated on the defined to activate its causal role.
4
Test a definition from Islamic sciences
Take a definition from fiqh, e.g., 'prayer is specific actions and words beginning with takbir and ending with taslim.' Apply the cause-based test: does knowledge of 'specific actions and words...' cause knowledge of 'prayer' when predicated on it? Likely yes.
This shows the practical use of the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ عَدَلَ عَنِ التَّعْبِيرِ بِـ «اللُّزُومِ» إِلَى التَّعْبِيرِ بِـ «السَّبَبِ»، فَقَالَ: «المُعَرِّفُ لِلشَّيْءِ: مَا تَكُونُ مَعْرِفَتُهُ سَبَباً لِمَعْرِفَةِ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْءٍ عِنْدَ حَمْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ»، فَيَخْرُجُ: المُتَضَايفَانِ؛ إِذْ لَيْسَ تَصَوُّرُ أحَدِهِمَا سَبَباً فِي تَصَوُّرِ الآخَرِ. وَالمُرَادُ بِـ «المَعْرِفَةِ»: تَصَوُّرُ الشَّيْءِ بِالكُنْهِ، أَوْ تَمْيِزِهِ عَنْ كُلِّ مَا سِوَاهُ [ج/ ١٧]، وَذَلِكَ كَ: «الحَيَوَانِ النَّاطِقِ»، فَإِنَّ تَصَوُّرَهُ يُوجِبُ تَصَوُّرَ مَاهِيَّةِ الإِنْسَانِ بِالكُنْهِ عِنْدَ حَمْلِهِ عَلَيْهَا؛ كَانْ يُقَالَ مَثَلاً: الإِنْسَانُ هُوَ: الحَيَوَانُ النَّاطِقُ، وَكَـ: «الصَّاحِكِ»، فَإِنَّ تَصَوُّرَهُ مَحْمُولاً عَلَى الإِنْسَانِ يُوجِبُ تَمَيَّزَ الإِنْسَانِ عَمَّا سِوَاهُ؛ لِكَوْنِ الصَّاحِكِ خَاصَّةٌ لَهُ. وَتَقْيِيدُ سَبَبِيَّتِهِ بِحَمْلِهِ عَلَى المُعَرَّفِ - بِالفَتْحِ - كَمَا ذَكَرْنَا لَا بُدَّ مِنْهُ؛ إِذْ قَدْ يُتَصَوَّرُ «الحَيَوَانُ النَّاطِقُ» وَيُجْهَلُ أَنَّهُ هُوَ مَاهِيَّةُ الإِنْسَانِ، فَلَا يَعْرِفُهُ إِلَّا بِحَمْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ. قَالَ السَّعْدُ: إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ الشَّيْءُ مُعَرِّفاً إِذَا اعْتُبِرَتْ نِسْبَتُهُ إِلَى المَظْلُوبِ تَعْرِيفُهُ؛ مِثْلَ: الجسْم النَّاطِقِ إِنِ اعْتُبِرَتْ نِسْبَتُهُ إِلَى الإِنْسَانِ، فَقَدْ أَفَادَ امْتِيَازَهُ عَنْ كُلِّ مَا عَدَاهُ، وَإِلَّا فَلَا نُسَلِّمُ أَنَّهُ مُعَرِّفٌ لَهُ. اهـ. وجواز التّعريف بالأخص أَوْلى مِنَ الأعم؛ إذ قربُ الأخصّ إلى المعرّف أكثر من قرب الأعم، والمتأخرون لما اشترطوا في المعرف الاطراد والانعكاس حكموا بأنَّ الأعم والأخص لا يصلحان للتعريف أصلاً، ولذلك عدل الكاتبيُّ عن تعريف الأقدمين إلى ما ذكره. ووجه شيخنا سيدي الطيب ما للمتأخرين: بأنَّ التَّعريف بالأعم أو الأخص يُوهم أنَّ ما هو خارج عن المعرَّف منه، وإن ما هو منه خارج عنه، فيوقع في الجهل، فيكون كالمغالطة في باب القياس، فيكون خطأ ممنوعاً يجب اجتنابه. قوله: (مَعْرِفَتُهُ سَبَباً لِمَعْرِفَةِ) المراد بـ «المعرفة الأولى: الحضور، وبالثانية: الحصولُ عن جهل؛ بمعنى أنَّ حضور الشَّيء بالبال محمولاً على المعرَّف - بفتح الراء ـ سبب لحصول معرفة الشَّيء المجهول، فإذا قيل: الإنسان هو الحَيَوَان النَّاطق»، فحضور «الحيوان الناطق» المعلومين أولاً محمولين على الإنسان» سببٌ لمعرفة حقيقة الإنسان المجهولة.
And among them is one who turned from expression with 'implication' to expression with 'cause', and said: 'The definer of a thing is that whose knowledge is a cause for knowledge of that thing when it is predicated upon it,' thus mutual correlatives are excluded; for neither's conception is a cause of the other's conception. And what is meant by 'knowledge' is conception of the thing in essence, or distinguishing it from everything else, like 'rational animal', for its conception necessitates conception of the essence of man in essence when predicated on it; as one says, for example: Man is the rational animal; and like 'the one who laughs', for its conception predicated on man necessitates distinguishing man from what is other than it, because laughing is a property of it. And restricting its causality to its predication on the defined—with fatha (the object)—as we mentioned is necessary; for one may conceive 'rational animal' yet be ignorant that it is the essence of man, so he does not know it except by predicating it upon him. Al-Sa'd said: 'A thing is only a definer when its relation to the sought definition is considered; like 'rational body' if its relation to man is considered, then it gave distinction from everything else, otherwise we do not accept that it is a definer of it.' End. And permissibility of definition by the more specific is preferable to the more general; for the closeness of the more specific to the defined is greater than the closeness of the more general. And the later scholars, when they required in the definer coextensiveness and converseness, judged that the more general and more specific are not suitable for definition at all, and for that reason al-Katibi turned from the definition of the ancients to what he mentioned. And our master Sayyid al-Tayyib explained the view of the later scholars: that definition by the more general or more specific gives the illusion that what is outside the defined is from it, and that what is from it is outside it, thus causing ignorance, so it is like a fallacy in the chapter of syllogism, and is an error that is prohibited and must be avoided. His statement: 'its knowledge is a cause for knowledge'—what is meant by the first 'knowledge' is presence, and by the second is acquisition after ignorance; meaning that the presence of the thing in the mind predicated on the defined—with fatha (the object)—is a cause for acquiring knowledge of the unknown thing. For if one says: 'Man is the rational animal,' then the presence of 'rational animal' as known first predicated on 'man' is a cause for knowing the unknown reality of man.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage presents an alternative definition of 'definer' using causality instead of implication, then discusses the debate between earlier and later scholars. The author first cites those who replace 'implication' (al-luzūm) with 'cause' (al-sabab), defining the definer as that whose knowledge, when predicated on the defined, causes knowledge of the defined. This excludes mutual correlatives as before. The passage illustrates with examples: 'rational animal' defines man in essence (complete definition), and 'the one who laughs' distinguishes man by property (incomplete definition). It emphasizes the need for the definer to be predicated on the defined to activate its defining function, as Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani noted. The discussion shifts to the permissibility of definition by a broader or narrower term. The earlier scholars (al-ʿAqdamūn) allowed it, but the later scholars (al-Mutaʾakhkhirūn), like al-Katibi, required coextensiveness (al-ʿippirād wal-inkisād), rejecting broader or narrower terms. The reason given by Sayyid al-Tayyib is that such definitions mislead, causing ignorance akin to a logical fallacy. Finally, the commentary clarifies that 'knowledge' in the definition means presence (in the mind) as cause for acquired knowledge.

Key Terms
المعرفة الأولى
المعرفة الثانية
المتضايفان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are mutual correlatives excluded from the cause-based definition of a definer?
A) Because they are too general.
B) Because knowledge of one does not cause knowledge of the other when predicated.
C) Because they are not used in definitions.
D) Because they were not mentioned by the ancients.

Key Takeaway
A definer is valid only if its knowledge, when predicated on the defined, causes knowledge of the defined.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Apply the cause-based definition to a fiqh term: is 'the specific actions and words beginning with takbir and ending with taslim' a valid definer for 'prayer'? Check if its knowledge, when predicated on 'prayer', causes knowledge of prayer's essence.
?
Take a mutual correlative pair from Arabic grammar (e.g., 'faʿil' and 'mafʿul') and explain why the cause-based definition excludes them.

The Shift: Later Scholars Require Coextensiveness in Definitions
Author compares ancients and later scholars on definition by broader/narrower terms, giving the latter's reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of earlier and later scholars on definition by broader or narrower terms, and identify why only coextensive terms are acceptable.

Core Idea
Later scholars require definers to be coextensive and convertible; broader or narrower terms cause ignorance.

The passage moves from a single definition to a historical debate: earlier scholars allowed defining a thing by a broader or narrower term, but later scholars imposed the stricter conditions of coextensiveness (al-ittirād) and converseness (al-inkisād). The reason, as explained by Sayyid al-Tayyib, is that such definitions mislead and are akin to fallacies. This shift shows how logic refined its standards over time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scholarly positions
Find the contrast between 'al-ʿAqdamūn' (ancients) who allowed definition by the more general (aʿamm) or more specific (akhass), and 'al-Mutaʾakhkhirūn' (later scholars) who rejected it.
The text says: 'and the later scholars when they required in the definer coextensiveness and converseness judged that the more general and more specific are not suitable for definition at all.'
2
Understand the requirement of coextensiveness and converseness
Coextensiveness (ittirād) means the definer applies to every instance of the defined; converseness (inkisād) means every instance of the definer is an instance of the defined. Together they guarantee mutual inclusion.
For example, 'rational animal' is coextensive with 'man' because every man is rational animal and vice versa.
3
See why broader or narrower terms fail
A broader term (e.g., 'animal' for man) includes more than man, so it does not convert. A narrower term (e.g., 'the one who laughs' for man) applies only to some men, so it is not coextensive. Such definitions give the illusion of inclusion/exclusion, causing ignorance.
Sayyid al-Tayyib's explanation: it 'gives the illusion that what is outside the defined is from it, and that what is from it is outside it.'
4
Apply the condition to an Islamic definition
Test the definition 'fasting is abstaining from food and drink' (which is broader because it excludes other abstentions like fasting from speech). Later scholars would reject it as a proper definition because it is not coextensive.
A proper definition would be 'fasting is intentional abstention from specific things (food, drink, marital relations) from dawn to sunset with intention.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بفتح الراء ـ سبب لحصول معرفة الشَّيء المجهول، فإذا قيل: الإنسان هو الحَيَوَان النَّاطق»، فحضور «الحيوان الناطق» المعلومين أولاً محمولين على الإنسان» سببٌ لمعرفة حقيقة الإنسان المجهولة.
And among them is one who turned from expression with 'implication' to expression with 'cause', and said: 'The definer of a thing is that whose knowledge is a cause for knowledge of that thing when it is predicated upon it,' thus mutual correlatives are excluded; for neither's conception is a cause of the other's conception. And what is meant by 'knowledge' is conception of the thing in essence, or distinguishing it from everything else, like 'rational animal', for its conception necessitates conception of the essence of man in essence when predicated on it; as one says, for example: Man is the rational animal; and like 'the one who laughs', for its conception predicated on man necessitates distinguishing man from what is other than it, because laughing is a property of it. And restricting its causality to its predication on the defined—with fatha (the object)—as we mentioned is necessary; for one may conceive 'rational animal' yet be ignorant that it is the essence of man, so he does not know it except by predicating it upon him. Al-Sa'd said: 'A thing is only a definer when its relation to the sought definition is considered; like 'rational body' if its relation to man is considered, then it gave distinction from everything else, otherwise we do not accept that it is a definer of it.' End. And permissibility of definition by the more specific is preferable to the more general; for the closeness of the more specific to the defined is greater than the closeness of the more general. And the later scholars, when they required in the definer coextensiveness and converseness, judged that the more general and more specific are not suitable for definition at all, and for that reason al-Katibi turned from the definition of the ancients to what he mentioned. And our master Sayyid al-Tayyib explained the view of the later scholars: that definition by the more general or more specific gives the illusion that what is outside the defined is from it, and that what is from it is outside it, thus causing ignorance, so it is like a fallacy in the chapter of syllogism, and is an error that is prohibited and must be avoided. Commentary
This passage presents an alternative definition of 'definer' using causality instead of implication, then discusses the debate between earlier and later scholars. Checkpoint
What is the main reason later scholars rejected definition by a more general or more specific term?
A) Such definitions were not used by earlier scholars.
B) They fail to satisfy coextensiveness and converseness, leading to ignorance.
C) They are too difficult to construct.
D) They are only valid for temporal things.

Key Takeaway
Proper definitions must be coextensive and convertible; otherwise they mislead and are epistemologically harmful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition 'ṣalāh is the act of bowing and prostrating.' Is this definition coextensive? (It is not, because bowing and prostrating occur outside prayer as well.) Construct a correct coextensive definition for ṣalāh using the conditions from the text.
?
Al-Katibi 'turned from the definition of the ancients to what he mentioned.' Based on the passage, what was the main problem with the ancients' approach? Explain in one sentence.

The Condition of Predication in Definition
Defense of predication condition in definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition of predication (haml) in a definition and explain why a definition without predication is invalid.

Core Idea
A definition is only valid if it is predicated on the defined thing.

In this passage, the commentator explains that a definition must be 'carried' (mahmul) on the defined thing. This is a key condition: if the definition is not predicated, it does not count as a definition. We will see how the author defends this condition against an objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Find in the Arabic where the author states that predication is a condition for a definition. Look for the phrase 'لفقد شرطه منه، وهو الحمل'.
2
Understand the example
The author uses 'Man is the rational animal' – the predication of 'rational animal' on 'man' gives knowledge of man's essence.
The same words 'rational animal' when not predicated do not constitute a definition.
3
Apply the condition to a new example
Consider defining 'wudu' as 'washing with water'. If you say 'Wudu is washing with water', it is predicated. If you just say 'washing with water' without reference to wudu, it is not a definition.
The condition is essential for the definition to fulfill its purpose.

Source Text

قوله : (مَعْرِفَتُهُ سَبَباً لِمَعْرِفَةِ) المراد بـ «المعرفة الأولى : الحضور، وبالثانية: الحصولُ عن جهل؛ بمعنى أنَّ حضور الشَّيء بالبال محمولاً على المعرَّف - بفتح الراء ـ سبب لحصول معرفة الشَّيء المجهول، فإذا قيل : الإنسان هو الحَيَوَان النَّاطق»، فحضور «الحيوان الناطق» المعلومين أولاً محمولين على الإنسان» سببٌ لمعرفة حقيقة الإنسان المجهولة. أَيْ: فَلَا يُقَالُ: إِنَّ التَّعْرِيفَ المَذْكُورَ غَيْرُ جَامِعٍ؛ لِخُرُوجِ نَحْوِ : «الحَيَوَانِ النَّاطِقِ مِنْهُ إِذَا كَانَ غَيْرَ مَحْمُولٍ عَلَى الإِنْسَانِ». لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ : إِنَّهُ حِينَئِذٍ لَا يَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهِ اسْمُ المُعَرِّفِ ؛ لِفَقْدِ شَرْطِهِ مِنْهُ، وَهُوَ الحَمْلُ . فَإِنْ قُلْتَ : هَلْ يَلْزَمُ فِي حَمْلِ الحَدِّ عَلَى المَحْدُودِ الحُكْمُ عَلَى الشَّيْءِ قَبْلَ تَصَوُّرِهِ؟ قُلْتُ : لَا يَلْزَمُ إِنَّمَا فِيهِ الحُكْمُ قَبْلَ التَّصْوِيرِ لِلغَيْرِ، وَهُوَ لَا يَضِرُّ . وَإنما قلنا ذلك؛ لأنَّا لو أردنا بالأولى : عن جهل، لَزِمَ التّعريف بمجهول، ولو كان المعرف . بفتحها - لا يحتاج إلى تحصيله عن جهل حال ،التَّعريف لزم تعريف المعلوم، وهو عبت؛ إلَّا أنَّ ما ذكر يلزم عليه استعمال لفظ المعرفة في معنيين هو فيهما حقيقة ومجاز، وسوّغ ذلك الاتكال على ما عُلِم مِن أنَّ المجهول لا يُعرف والمعلوم لا يعرف فكان ذلك كالقرينة على المراد. قوله : (قُلْتُ : لَا يَلْزَمُ، إِنَّمَا فِيهِ الحُكْمُ ... إلخ) معناه : أنَّ الحاء ما حكم على الإنسان بكذا إلَّا حيث تصوّر الإنسان؛ إذ الحكم على الشَّيء فرع تصوره. نعم ؛ ؛ الغير المحدود له لا يتصوّره إلا بعد هذا الحكم الحاصل مِنَ الحاد، ففيه الحكم قبل التّصوير للغير الذي هو المحدود له، وذلك لا يضرُّ، وفيما تضمنه كلام هذا الشارح مِن أنَّ الحاد يحكم على المحدود بالحدِّ نظر ؛ إذ لا حكم في الحد أصلاً ؛ لأنَّ الحاد ينقشُ في الذهن صورة المحدود ويصوِّرُها ، فإذا قال: الإنسان هو : الحَيَوَان النَّاطق، لم يقصد حكماً، وإلا كان مصدقاً لا مصوّراً . هذا بالنسبة للحاد، أما المحدود له، فلا يحكم على الإنسان» بشيء إلا حيث انتقشت صورته في ذهنه وتصورها من تلقاء الحاد، فهو إذا حكم لم يحكم إلا بعد النَّصور، فاندفع السُّؤال والجواب، والله تعالى أعلم بالصواب. وهذا معنى ما نقله شيخنا ابن منصور عن ياسين مِن : أنَّ هذا الحمل إنَّما هو صوري ولا تصديق ولا حكم، بل هو تصوير ونقش في صحيفة الذهن، ولهذا لا يتوجه عليه منع كما يأتي، وبه تعلم ما وقع للشيخ اليوسي في «حواشي المختصر».
His saying: 'Its knowledge is a cause for knowledge' – the intended meaning of 'first knowledge' is presence, and 'second knowledge' is acquisition from ignorance; meaning that the presence of the thing in the mind, predicated upon the defined (with fatha on the ra), is a cause for obtaining knowledge of the unknown thing. So when it is said: 'Man is the rational animal', then the presence of 'rational animal', both known first, predicated upon 'man', is a cause for knowledge of the unknown reality of man. That is, it should not be said that the aforementioned definition is not comprehensive, due to the exclusion of something like 'rational animal' from it when it is not predicated upon 'man'. Because we say: In that case, the name 'definition' does not apply to it, due to the absence of its condition, which is predication. If you say: Does the predication of the definition upon the defined necessitate a judgment about the thing before its conceptualization? I say: It does not necessitate; rather, in it there is judgment before conceptualization for the other person, and that does not harm. And we only said that because if we intended by 'first' [knowledge] 'from ignorance', definition by an unknown would be necessary, and if the definiendum does not need to be acquired from ignorance at the time of definition, definition of the known would be necessary, which is absurd; except that what is mentioned necessitates the use of the word 'knowledge' in two meanings – one literal and one metaphorical – and that is permitted by relying on what is known: that the unknown is not known and the known is not defined, so that becomes a contextual indicator of the intended meaning. His saying: 'I say: It does not necessitate, rather in it there is judgment... etc.' – its meaning is that the judge does not judge about man with something except when he has conceptualized man, since judgment about a thing is a branch of its conceptualization. Yes, the other person, the one being defined for, does not conceptualize it except after this judgment obtained from the definer, so in it there is judgment before conceptualization for the other, the one being defined for, and that does not harm. And in what the speech of this commentator contains, that the definer judges about the defined by the definition, there is scrutiny; because there is no judgment in definition at all, because the definer inscribes in the mind the form of the defined and conceptualizes it, so when he says 'Man is the rational animal', he does not intend a judgment, otherwise he would be a declarer, not a conceptualizer. This is regarding the definer. As for the one being defined for, he does not judge about 'man' with anything except when its form is inscribed in his mind and he conceptualizes it from the definer's initiation; so when he judges, he only judges after conceptualization. Thus the question and answer are repelled. And Allah knows best what is correct. And this is the meaning of what our teacher Ibn Mansur transmitted from Yasin: that this predication is merely formal (suri), not a declaration nor a judgment, but rather a conceptualization and an inscription on the tablet of the mind, and for that reason it does not invite prevention as will come, and by it you know what occurred to al-Yusi in his glosses on al-Mukhtasar.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from al-Sullam al-Murawnaq defining 'definition' (mu'arraf). The commentator (al-Bannani) clarifies the condition that a definition must be predicated (mahmul) upon the defined thing (al-mu'arraf bi al-fath). The first knowledge refers to the mental presence of the definition; the second is the acquisition of knowledge of the unknown thing. Using the example 'Man is the rational animal', the presence of 'rational animal' (known beforehand) predicated on 'man' gives knowledge of man's essence. The first objection says: then the definition would not be comprehensive because if 'rational animal' is not predicated on 'man' (e.g., when considered in isolation), it is excluded. The answer: in that case it does not qualify as a definition because the condition of predication is missing. The second objection asks: does predication require a judgment about the thing before it is conceptualized? The answer: the judgment is only for the benefit of the learner (al-ghayr), i.e., the one being taught; the definer already has the concept. The commentator then refines the discussion: the earlier commentator (al-Akhdari?) claimed that the definer makes a judgment, but this is scrutinized because definition is purely conceptual (tasawwur), not declarative (tasdiq). The definer inscribes the form; there is no judgment. For the learner, judgment only occurs after conceptualization. Thus the objection is invalid. He then cites Ibn Mansur and Yasin to confirm that the predication is formal (suri) and not a judgment. This guards against the misunderstanding that definition involves a hukm.

Key Terms
المعرف
الحمل
المعرف بفتح الراء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the utterance 'rational animal' not qualify as a definition of 'man' when it is not predicated on 'man'?
A) Because it is not comprehensive (ghayr jami').
B) Because the condition of predication (haml) is missing.
C) Because 'rational animal' is too general.
D) Because it requires a judgment before conceptualization.

Key Takeaway
Predication (haml) is an essential condition for a definition to be valid; without it, the utterance is not a definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the definition 'Salah is the specific acts of worship with takbir and taslim.' Explain why the phrase 'specific acts of worship with takbir and taslim' would not be a definition of salah if it were not predicated on salah.
?
Identify another definition from fiqh (e.g., definition of 'zakah') and verify that it is predicated on the defined term.

Definition as Conceptualization, Not Judgment
Refutation of the objection that predication implies judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conceptualization (tasawwur) and judgment (tasdiq) in definition and explain why definition does not involve a judgment.

Core Idea
Definition is pure conceptualization; the definer does not judge, but inscribes a mental image.

The passage addresses a subtle point: when the definer says 'Man is the rational animal', does he make a judgment? The commentator argues that this is only a formal predication, not a judgment. Definition belongs to conceptualization (tasawwur), not assent (tasdiq). This is crucial to avoid confusion between defining and declaring.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find in the Arabic the objection: 'هل يلزم في حمل الحد على المحدود الحكم على الشيء قبل تصوره؟'
This asks whether predication requires a judgment before conceptualization.
2
Understand the answer
The author says 'لا يلزم' and explains that the judgment is for the benefit of the learner, not the definer. The definer already has the concept.
3
Grasp the refinement
The commentator then refines: the definer does not judge at all. He 'inscribes the form in the mind' (ينقش في الذهن صورة المحدود). Definition is conceptualization, not declaration.
If the definer intended a judgment, he would be a declarer (musaddiq), not a conceptualizer (musawwir).
4
Apply the distinction
Consider the learner: he only judges after conceptualization. So the objection that predication requires prior judgment is invalid.
This preserves the purity of definition as conceptual.

Defending the Comprehensiveness of a Definition
Responding to an objection on definition comprehensiveness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how a definition is defended against an objection of non-comprehensiveness by invoking the condition of predication.

Core Idea
A definition's comprehensiveness is conditional upon predication.

In this passage, the commentator responds to a potential objection that a definition might exclude some instances. He clarifies that if a term is not predicated of the definiendum, it does not qualify as a definition. This lesson unpacks the logical move of invoking the condition of predication to defend a definition's completeness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection claims the definition is not comprehensive because something like 'rational animal' could be excluded if not predicated of 'human'.
The example given is 'الحيوان الناطق' (rational animal) not predicated of 'الإنسان' (human).
2
Analyze the response
The commentator says that if it is not predicated, the term fails to be a definition because predication is a necessary condition.
The condition is stated as 'الحمل' (predication).
3
Extract the logical principle
A definition must be predicable of its definiendum. If it is not, it is excluded from the definition's scope.
4
Apply to another example
Consider the definition of 'qiyas' in usul al-fiqh. If a specific case cannot be predicated of qiyas, does that affect the definition's comprehensiveness? The same condition applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المعرفات أَيْ: فَلَا يُقَالُ: إِنَّ التَّعْرِيفَ المَذْكُورَ غَيْرُ جَامِعٍ؛ لِخُرُوجِ نَحْوِ: «الحَيَوَانِ النَّاطِقِ مِنْهُ إِذَا كَانَ غَيْرَ مَحْمُولٍ عَلَى الإِنْسَانِ». لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ: إِنَّهُ حِينَئِذٍ لَا يَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهِ اسْمُ المُعَرِّفِ؛ لِفَقْدِ شَرْطِهِ مِنْهُ، وَهُوَ الحَمْلُ. فَإِنْ قُلْتَ: هَلْ يَلْزَمُ فِي حَمْلِ الحَدِّ عَلَى المَحْدُودِ الحُكْمُ عَلَى الشَّيْءِ قَبْلَ تَصَوُّرِهِ؟ قُلْتُ: لَا يَلْزَمُ إِنَّمَا فِيهِ الحُكْمُ قَبْلَ التَّصْوِيرِ لِلغَيْرِ، وَهُوَ لَا يَضِرُّ. وَإِنَّمَا قُلْنَا ذَلِكَ؛ لِأَنَّا لَوْ أَرَدْنَا بِالأُولَى عَنْ جَهْلٍ، لَزِمَ التَّعْرِيفُ بِمَجْهُولٍ، وَلَوْ كَانَ المُعَرِّفُ بِفَتْحِهَا لَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى تَحْصِيلِهِ عَنْ جَهْلٍ حَالَ التَّعْرِيفِ لَزِمَ تَعْرِيفُ المَعْلُومِ، وَهُوَ عَبَثٌ؛ إِلَّا أَنَّ مَا ذُكِرَ يَلْزَمُ عَلَيْهِ اسْتِعْمَالُ لَفْظِ المَعْرِفَةِ فِي مَعْنَيَيْنِ هُوَ فِيهِمَا حَقِيقَةٌ وَمَجَازٌ، وَسَوَّغَ ذَلِكَ الاتِّكَالُ عَلَى مَا عُلِمَ مِنْ أَنَّ المَجْهُولَ لَا يُعْرَفُ وَالمَعْلُومَ لَا يُعَرَّفُ فَكَانَ ذَلِكَ كَالْقَرِينَةِ عَلَى المُرَادِ. قَوْلُهُ: (قُلْتُ: لَا يَلْزَمُ، إِنَّمَا فِيهِ الحُكْمُ ... إلخ) مَعْنَاهُ: أَنَّ الحَادَّ مَا حَكَمَ عَلَى الإِنْسَانِ بِكَذَا إِلَّا حَيْثُ تَصَوَّرَ الإِنْسَانَ؛ إِذِ الحُكْمُ عَلَى الشَّيْءِ فَرْعُ تَصَوُّرِهِ. نَعَمْ؛ الغَيْرُ المَحْدُودُ لَهُ لَا يَتَصَوَّرُهُ إِلَّا بَعْدَ هَذَا الحُكْمِ الحَاصِلِ مِنَ الحَادِّ، فَفِيهِ الحُكْمُ قَبْلَ التَّصْوِيرِ لِلغَيْرِ الَّذِي هُوَ المَحْدُودُ لَهُ، وَذَلِكَ لَا يَضُرُّ. وَفِيمَا تَضَمَّنَهُ كَلَامُ هَذَا الشَّارِحِ مِنْ أَنَّ الحَادَّ يَحْكُمُ عَلَى المَحْدُودِ بِالحَدِّ نَظَرٌ؛ إِذْ لَا حُكْمَ فِي الحَدِّ أَصْلًا؛ لِأَنَّ الحَادَّ يَنْقُشُ فِي الذِّهْنِ صُورَةَ المَحْدُودِ وَيُصَوِّرُهَا، فَإِذَا قَالَ: الإِنْسَانُ هُوَ: الحَيَوَانُ النَّاطِقُ، لَمْ يَقْصِدْ حُكْمًا، وَإِلَّا كَانَ مُصَدِّقًا لَا مُصَوِّرًا. هَذَا بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلْحَادِّ، أَمَّا المَحْدُودُ لَهُ، فَلَا يَحْكُمُ عَلَى الإِنْسَانِ بِشَيْءٍ إِلَّا حَيْثُ انْتَقَشَتْ صُورَتُهُ فِي ذِهْنِهِ وَتَصَوَّرَهَا مِنْ تِلْقَاءِ الحَادِّ، فَهُوَ إِذَا حَكَمَ لَمْ يَحْكُمْ إِلَّا بَعْدَ التَّصَوُّرِ، فَانْدَفَعَ السُّؤَالُ وَالجَوَابُ، وَاللَّهُ تَعَالَى أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوَابِ. وَهَذَا مَعْنَى مَا نَقَلَهُ شَيْخُنَا ابْنُ مَنْصُورٍ عَنْ يَاسِينَ مِنْ: أَنَّ هَذَا الحَمْلَ إِنَّمَا هُوَ صُورِيٌّ وَلَا تَصْدِيقَ وَلَا حُكْمَ، بَلْ هُوَ تَصْوِيرٌ وَنَقْشٌ فِي صَحِيفَةِ الذِّهْنِ، وَلِهَذَا لَا يَتَوَجَّهُ عَلَيْهِ مَنْعٌ كَمَا يَأْتِي، وَبِهِ تُعْلَمُ مَا وَقَعَ لِلشَّيْخِ اليُوسِيِّ فِي «حَوَاشِي المُخْتَصَرِ».
Section on definients. Meaning: So it is not said that the mentioned definition is not comprehensive due to the exclusion of something like 'the rational animal' from it when it is not predicated of 'human'. Because we say: Then the name 'definient' does not apply to it due to the lack of its condition, which is predication. If you say: Is it necessary in predicating the definition on the definiendum to judge the thing before its conceptualization? I say: It is not necessary; rather, in it there is judgment before conceptualization for the other [person], and that does not harm. And we only said that because if we intended by the first [word] 'from ignorance', the definition by something unknown would follow, and if the definient (with fat-ha) did not need to be obtained from ignorance at the time of definition, the definition of the known would follow, which is futile; except that what was mentioned would necessitate using the word 'knowledge' in two meanings in which it is literal and metaphorical, and that was justified by reliance on what is known that the unknown is not known and the known is not defined, so that became like a clue to the intended meaning. His statement: ('I say: It is not necessary; rather, in it there is judgment... etc.') meaning: The definer does not judge of 'human' something except where he has conceptualized 'human', since judgment on a thing is a branch of its conceptualization. Yes, the other person (the learner) does not conceptualize it except after this judgment obtained from the definer, so in it there is judgment before conceptualization for the other who is the learner, and that does not harm. And in what the statement of this commentator contains that the definer judges on the definiendum with the definition, there is consideration; because there is no judgment in the definition at all; because the definer engraves in the mind the image of the definiendum and depicts it. So when he says: 'Human is: the rational animal', he did not intend a judgment, otherwise he would be an asserter (musaddiq) not a depictor (musawwir). This is regarding the definer. As for the learner, he does not judge of 'human' anything except when its image is engraved in his mind and he conceptualizes it from the direction of the definer. So when he judges, he only judges after conceptualization. Thus the question and answer are repelled. And God Most High knows best the truth. And this is the meaning of what our master Ibn Mansur transmitted from Yasin: that this predication is merely formal (suri) and there is no assent (tasdiq) nor judgment, but rather it is a depiction and engraving in the tablet of the mind. For this reason no objection can be directed against it as will come. And by it you know what occurred to al-Yusi in his glosses on 'al-Mukhtasar'.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that defends a definition against an objection and clarifies the role of judgment in definition. The commentator begins by responding to a potential objection: the definition might be considered non-comprehensive because something like 'rational animal' (which is actually the definition of human) would be excluded if it is not predicated of 'human' in a specific instance. The response is that if it is not predicated, then it does not satisfy the condition of being a definition, so the definition still holds. Then a deeper question arises: does predicating a definition on the definiendum require a judgment (hukm) prior to conceptualization (tasawwur)? The answer distinguishes between the definer and the learner. The definer, when stating the definition, is not making a judgment but rather depicting the essence; judgment would belong to the realm of assent (tasdiq). The learner, however, only judges after conceptualizing the definiendum from the definer's depiction. Thus, no problematic circularity occurs. The commentator further explains that using the term 'knowledge' (ma'rifa) in two senses (for the unknown and the known) is justified by context. Finally, he endorses Ibn Mansur's transmission from Yasin that the predication in definition is merely formal (suri) with no truth-claim, thus immune to certain objections. This lesson guards against the misunderstanding that definition involves an assertive judgment.

Key Terms
الحاد
المحدود
المعرف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the definition not rendered non-comprehensive by the exclusion of 'rational animal' when not predicated of 'human'?
A) Because 'rational animal' is not a definition.
B) Because predication is a necessary condition for being a definition.
C) Because the definition is for 'human' only.
D) Because the objection is invalid.

Key Takeaway
A definition's comprehensiveness is evaluated based on its predication condition, not on exhaustive enumeration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Examine the definition of 'qiyas' in al-Ghazali's al-Mustasfa. Does it satisfy the condition of predication? Provide a scenario where a specific analogy is not predicated of qiyas and explain whether that affects the definition's comprehensiveness.

10 min
Judgment and Conceptualization in Definition
Clarifying the role of judgment in definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the roles of judgment (hukm) and conceptualization (tasawwur) in definition, and explain why the definer does not make a judgment.

Core Idea
Definition is pure depiction, not assertion.

A key objection in logic is whether defining involves a prior judgment. This passage clarifies that the definer merely engraves a concept; judgment occurs only in the learner's mind after conceptualization. Understanding this distinction preserves the purity of definition as a tool for conceptualization.

Guided Path
1
Locate the question
Find the question: 'Is it necessary in predicating the definition on the definiendum to judge the thing before its conceptualization?'
The question appears right after the response to the comprehensiveness objection.
2
Distinguish definer and learner
The response separates the definer's action from the learner's. The definer does not judge; he depicts. The learner judges only after conceptualizing.
3
Understand 'no judgment in definition'
The commentator asserts that when the definer says 'Human is rational animal', he is not asserting a proposition but depicting an essence.
This is reinforced by the statement that the definer would be a musaddiq (asserter) if he intended judgment.
4
Apply to tasawwur vs tasdiq
Definition belongs to tasawwur (conceptualization), not tasdiq (assent). This distinction is foundational in Islamic logic.
The passage explicitly uses the terms تصور and تصديق.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لَا يُعَرَّفُ فَكَانَ ذَلِكَ كَالْقَرِينَةِ عَلَى المُرَادِ. قَوْلُهُ: (قُلْتُ: لَا يَلْزَمُ، إِنَّمَا فِيهِ الحُكْمُ ... إلخ) مَعْنَاهُ: أَنَّ الحَادَّ مَا حَكَمَ عَلَى الإِنْسَانِ بِكَذَا إِلَّا Section on definients. Meaning: So it is not said that the mentioned definition is not comprehensive due to the exclusion of something like 'the rational animal' from it when it is not predicated of 'human'. Because we say: Then the name 'definient' does not apply to it due to the lack of its condition, which is predication. If you say: Is it necessary in predicating the definition on the definiendum to judge the thing before its conceptualization? I say: It is not necessary; rather, in it there is judgment before conceptualization for the other [person], and that does not harm. And we only said that because if we intended by the first [word] 'from ignorance', the definition by something unknown would follow, and if the definient (with fat-ha) did not need to be obtained from ignorance at the time of definition, the definition of the known would follow, which is futile; except that what was mentioned would necessitate using the word 'knowledge' in two meanings in which it is literal and metaphorical, and that was justified by reliance on what is known that the unknown is not known and the known is not defined, so that became like a clue to the intended meaning. His statement: ('I say: It is not necessary; rather, in it there is judgment... etc.') meaning: The definer does not judge of 'human' something except where he has conceptualized 'human', since judgment on a thing is a branch of its conceptualization. Yes, the other person (the learner) does not conceptualize it except after this judgment obtained from the definer, so in it there is judgment before conceptualization for the other who is the learner, and that does not harm. And in what the statement of this commentator contains that the definer judges on the definiendum with the definition, there is consideration; because there is no judgment in the definition at all; because the definer engraves in the mind the image of the definiendum and depicts it. So when he says: 'Human is: the rational animal', he did not intend a judgment, otherwise he would be an asserter (musaddiq) not a depictor (musawwir). This is regarding the definer. As for the learner, he does not judge of 'human' anything except when its image is engraved in his mind and he conceptualizes it from the direction of the definer. So when he judges, he only judges after conceptualization. Thus the question and answer are repelled. And God Most High knows best the truth. And this is the meaning of what our master Ibn Mansur transmitted from Yasin: that this predication is merely formal (suri) and there is no assent (tasdiq) nor judgment, but rather it is a depiction and engraving in the tablet of the mind. For this reason no objection can be directed against it as will come. And by it you know what occurred to al-Yusi in his glosses on 'al-Mukhtasar'.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that defends a definition against an objection and clarifies the role of judgment in definition. The commentator begins by responding to a potential objection: the definition might be considered non-comprehensive because something like 'rational animal' (which is actually the definition of human) would be excluded if it is not predicated of 'human' in a specific instance. The response is that if it is not predicated, then it does not satisfy the condition of being a definition, so the definition still holds. Then a deeper question arises: does predicating a definition on the definiendum require a judgment (hukm) prior to conceptualization (tasawwur)? The answer distinguishes between the definer and the learner. The definer, when stating the definition, is not making a judgment but rather depicting the essence; judgment would belong to the realm of assent (tasdiq). The learner, however, only judges after conceptualizing the definiendum from the definer's depiction. Thus, no problematic circularity occurs. The commentator further explains that using the term 'knowledge' (ma'rifa) in two senses (for the unknown and the known) is justified by context. Finally, he endorses Ibn Mansur's transmission from Yasin that the predication in definition is merely formal (suri) with no truth-claim, thus immune to certain objections. This lesson guards against the misunderstanding that definition involves an assertive judgment.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when the definer says 'Human is the rational animal', does he make a judgment (hukm)?
A) Yes, because he predicates something of human.
B) No, because he is only depicting a concept.
C) Yes, but only for the learner.
D) No, because the learner judges instead.

Key Takeaway
Definition belongs to tasawwur (conceptualization) and does not involve tasdiq (assent).

The Principle of Mugayara: Definiens Must Differ from Definiendum
Author derives that definiens must differ from definiendum and explains types of difference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the type of mugayara (difference) between a definiens and definiendum in a given definition.

Core Idea
The definiens must be other than the definiendum in concept or presentation, not necessarily in reference.

This passage establishes a foundational principle for all definitions: the definiens cannot be identical to the definiendum in every respect. If it were, definition would be circular or useless. The author explains how this 'otherness' (mugayara) is realized in different types of definitions—complete, incomplete, description, and even verbal definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key claim
Find where the author states that the definiens must be other than the definiendum. This is the central principle: 'al-mu'arraf li al-mahiyya la budda an yakuna ghayraha'.
The reason given is that knowledge of the definiens causes knowledge of the definiendum, and a cause is other than its effect.
2
Distinguish types of mugayara
The passage outlines two main types of mugayara: difference in concept (mafhum) and difference in presentation (ijmal/tafsil). Note how these correspond to different definition types.
Complete definition differs in presentation (detail vs. summary); incomplete definition and description differ in concept.
3
Analyze the complete definition (hadd tamm)
The complete definition indicates the quiddity in detail (tafsilan), while the definiendum observes it in summary (ijmalan). This difference in the mode of presentation is sufficient for mugayara.
This resolves the apparent identity: the definiens is the same quiddity but articulated differently.
4
Analyze incomplete definition and description
In hadd naqis, only some essential attributes are mentioned, so the part differs conceptually from the whole. In rasm, a property (khassa) like 'the writer' has a different concept from the essence ('human').
The union in reference (mitsdaq) does not require union in concept.
5
Address the synonym objection
For verbal definitions (ta'rif lafzi) like defining 'human' by 'bashar', the mugayara is merely verbal, not conceptual. The condition is only that the definiens is more famous (ashhariyya).
The commentator notes this is accepted by al-Yusi and Qadura, and criticizes the author of al-Nihaya for misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُؤْخَذُ مِنَ التَّعْرِيفِ المَذْكُورِ أُمُوراً: أَحَدُهَا: أَنَّ المُعَرِّفَ لِلمَاهِيَّةِ لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ غَيْرُهَا؛ لأَنَّ مَعْرِفَتَهُ سَبَبُ لِمَعْرِفَتِهَا، وَالسَّبَبُ غَيْرُ المُسَبَّبِ، وَوَجْهُ المُغَايَرَةِ فِي الحَدِّ التَّامِّ: أَنَّهُ دَالٌّ عَلَى المَاهِيَّةِ تَفْصِيلاً، وَالمَحْدُودُ تُلَاحَظُ مِنْهُ المَاهِيَّةُ إِجْمَالاً، وَاخْتِلَافُ الاِعْتِبَارِ بِالإِجْمَالِ وَالتَّفْصِيلِ كَافٍ فِي المُغَايَرَةِ. وَأَمَّا الحَدُّ النَّاقِصُ وَالرَّسْمُ مُطْلَقاً، فَوَجْهُ المُغَايَرَةِ بَيْنَهُمَا وَبَيْنَ المَاهِيَّةِ وَاضِحٌ، فَالتَّعْرِيفُ وَالمُعَرَّفُ مَعَ اتِّحَادِهِمَا فِي المَصْدُوقِ هُمَا مُخْتَلِفَانِ تَارَةً بِالمَفْهُومِ، وَتَارَةً بِالإِجْمَالِ وَالتَّفْصِيلِ. فَإِنْ قُلْتَ: مَا وَجْهُ المُغَايَرَةِ فِي تَعْرِيفِ أَحَدِ المُتَرَادِفَيْنِ بِالآخَرِ كَتَعْرِيفِ الإِنْسَانِ بـ: «البَشَرِ إِذَا كَانَ اسْمُ البَشَرِ أَشْهَرَ مِنْهُ؟ قَوْلُهُ: (لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ غَيْرُهَا) مُرَادُهُ: أَنْ يَكُونَ بَيْنَهُمَا مُغَايَرَةٌ فِي المَعْنَى مِنْ وَجْهٍ مَّا مَعَ الاتِّحَادِ فِي المَصْدُوقِ، لَا المُغَايَرَةُ فِي اللَّفْظِ فَقَطْ، وَبِهِ تُعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ لَا تَنَافِيَ بَيْنَ كَوْنِ الحَدِّ مُغَايِراً لِلْمَحْدُودِ وَبَيْنَ كَوْنِهِمَا مُتَّحِدَيْنِ؛ إِذِ الحَدُّ التَّامُّ مَثَلاً هُوَ نَفْسُ المَحْدُودِ. قَوْلُهُ: (وَاضِحٌ) بَيَانُهُ: أَنَّ الحَدَّ النَّاقِصَ إِنَّمَا يُذْكَرُ فِيهِ بَعْضُ الذَّاتِيَّاتِ، وَيُتْرَكُ فِيهِ ذِكْرُ البَعْضِ، وَالبَعْضُ مُغَايِرٌ لِلْكُلِّ مَفْهُوماً، وَإِنْ سَاوَاهُ مَصْدُوقاً، وَالرَّسْمُ يَكُونُ بِالخَاصَّةِ وَحْدَهَا، أَوْ مَعَ الجِنْسِ، وَالخَوَاصُّ مُغَايِرَةٌ لِلْمُخْتَصِّ بِهَا مَفْهُوماً كَـ«الْكَاتِبِ» مَثَلاً لَـ«الإِنْسَانِ»، فَمَفْهُومُهُ يُفِيدُ مَا لَا إِشْعَارَ لِلإِنْسَانِ بِهِ. قَوْلُهُ: (فَإِنْ قُلْتَ ... إلخ) حَاصِلُ هَذَا الإِيرَادِ أَنَّ التَّعْرِيفَ اللَّفْظِيَّ لَا يُتَعَقَّلُ فِيهِ إِجْمَالٌ وَلَا تَفْصِيلٌ، فَلَا مُغَايَرَةَ بَيْنَهُمَا. وَجَوَابُهُ أَنَّ المُعَرِّفَ اللَّفْظِيَّ لَيْسَتْ فِيهِ مُغَايَرَةٌ فِي المَعْنَى؛ لأنَّ المَقْصُودَ مِنْهُ بَيَانُ المَدْلُولِ اللُّغَوِيِّ، وَإِنَّمَا فِيهِ المُغَايَرَةُ اللَّفْظِيَّةُ، وَهِيَ فِيهِ كَافِيَةٌ، وَإِنَّمَا اشْتَرَطُوا لَهُ الأَشْهَرِيَّةَ فَقَطْ، كَمَا حَقَّقَهُ اليُوسِيُّ وَسَلَّمَهُ لَهُ هَذَا الشَّارِحُ فِي «حَوَاشِي المُخْتَصَرِ»، وَأَوْمَأَ إِلَيْهِ قَدُورَةُ. وَأَمَّا قَوْلُهُ هُنَا: (قُلْتُ: يَأْتِي ... إلخ) فَفِيهِ نَظَرٌ؛ لأَنَّهُ بَنَاهُ عَلَى مَا تَوَهَّمَهُ صَاحِبُ «النِّهَايَةِ».
And from the mentioned definition are taken several matters. One of them: That the definiens of the quiddity must be other than it; because knowledge of it is a cause of knowledge of it, and the cause is other than the effect. And the aspect of difference (mugayara) in the complete definition (hadd tamm) is that it indicates the quiddity in detail (tafsilan), while from the definiendum the quiddity is observed in summary (ijmalan). And the difference of consideration (i'tibar) between summary and detail is sufficient for otherness. As for the incomplete definition (hadd naqis) and the description (rasm) absolutely, the aspect of difference between them and the quiddity is clear. So the definition (ta'rif) and the definiendum, despite their union in reference (mitsdaq), are different sometimes in concept (mafhum) and sometimes in summary and detail. If you say: What is the aspect of difference in defining one of two synonyms by the other, like defining 'human' by 'bashar' when the name 'bashar' is more famous than it? His statement: ('It must be other than it') means: There must be a difference in meaning between them in some respect despite union in reference, not merely a difference in wording. And by it you know that there is no contradiction between the definition being other than the definiendum and them being united; since the complete definition, for example, is the same as the definiendum. His statement: ('clear') Its explanation: The incomplete definition only mentions some of the essential attributes (dhatiyyat) and leaves out mentioning some, and the part is different from the whole in concept even if it equals it in reference. And the description (rasm) is by the property (khassa) alone or with the genus, and properties are different from what they are specific to in concept, like 'the writer' for example for 'human', so its concept conveys what 'human' does not indicate. His statement: ('If you say... etc.') The gist of this objection is that verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) does not involve either summary or detail, so there is no difference between them. And its answer is that the verbal definiens has no difference in meaning; because the intent of it is to explain the linguistic signification; rather, there is only verbal difference in it, and that is sufficient for it. And they only stipulated for it being more famous (ashhariyya), as al-Yusi verified and this commentator accepted from him in his glosses on 'al-Mukhtasar', and Qadura hinted at it. As for his statement here: ('I say: it comes... etc.') there is consideration; because he built it on what the author of 'al-Nihaya' imagined.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage derives several principles about definitions from the earlier discussion. The first principle: The definiens must be other than the definiendum (the quiddity) because knowledge of the definiens causes knowledge of the definiendum, and a cause is other than its effect. The difference (mugayara) in a complete definition (hadd tamm) is a difference of consideration: the definiens expresses the quiddity in detail (tafsil), while the definiendum is observed in summary (ijmal). This difference in the mode of presentation suffices for otherness. For an incomplete definition (hadd naqis) and a description (rasm), the otherness is obvious: the incomplete definition gives only some essential parts (dhatiyyat), and a part is conceptually distinct from the whole even if they refer to the same thing; a description uses a property (khassa) like 'the writer' for 'human', which has a different concept. The author then addresses an objection about synonym definitions: if we define 'human' by 'bashar', which are synonyms, how is there any difference? The answer is that in a verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi), the difference is not in meaning but only in wording, and the only condition is that the definiens is more famous (ashhariyya) than the definiendum. The commentator notes that this has been verified by al-Yusi and accepted by the author. He also critiques a statement by the author of 'al-Nihaya' for misunderstanding this point. This lesson guards against the misunderstanding that definiens and definiendum are identical in every respect; they can differ conceptually or in the mode of presentation.

Key Terms

الماهية
الحد التام
الحد الناقص
الرسم
المغايرة
المصدوق

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the mugayara in a complete definition (hadd tamm)?
A) They differ in reference (mitsdaq).
B) They differ in concept (mafhum).
C) They differ in presentation (detail vs summary).
D) They differ both in concept and reference.

Key Takeaway
The definiens and definiendum can be united in reference (mitsdaq) yet differ in concept or presentation, and this mugayara is necessary for a valid definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: In the definition of 'riba' as 'excess without compensation in a barter of certain types of goods', identify the type of mugayara between the definiens and the definiendum. Is it conceptual or presentational?
?

First Condition: Definiens Must Be Other than Definiendum
Author explains and justifies the first condition of definition: the definiens must be other than the definiendum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the required difference (mughāyara) between definiens and definiendum in complete definitions, incomplete definitions, and descriptions, using the criteria of meaning and mode of presentation.

Core Idea
The definiens and definiendum are one in reference, but two in concept.

This lesson clarifies the first condition every definition must satisfy: the definiens must be different from the definiendum. But what kind of difference? As the text shows, it is a difference in meaning and conceptual content, not a mere difference in wording. Understanding this condition is essential for constructing valid definitions in any Islamic science, from fiqh to kalām.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition being derived.
The author states that from the definition (al-ta'rif) we derive several matters, the first being that the definiens must be other than the definiendum. Locate this sentence in the Arabic: 'وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنَ التَّعْرِيفِ المَذْكُورِ أُمُوراً : أَحَدُهَا : أَنَّ المُعَرِّفَ لِلمَاهِيَّةِ لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ غَيْرُهَا'.
2
Understand the causal reasoning.
The author gives a reason: knowledge of the definiens is a cause for knowledge of the definiendum, and a cause is other than its effect. This reasoning grounds the condition in cause-effect logic. Notice how the logic of 'cause and effect' is used to justify the condition.
3
Examine the difference in the complete definition (ḥadd tāmm).
The text explains that the complete definition indicates the essence in detail (tafṣīl), while the defined is observed in summary (ijmāl). This difference in mode of presentation is sufficient for otherness. Example: 'rational animal' (definiens) vs. 'human' (definiendum): both refer to the same essence, but the definition spells it out while the term 'human' is a summary.
4
Compare with incomplete definitions and descriptions.
For the incomplete definition (ḥadd nāqiṣ), only part of the essence is mentioned, so part vs. whole is obviously a difference in concept. For description (rasm), the property (like 'writer' for 'human') is conceptually different from the defined. The text says the difference is 'clear' in these cases.
5
Distinguish difference in meaning vs. wording.
The gloss clarifies that the required difference is in meaning (ma'nā), not just in wording. The definiens and definiendum may have the same referent (unity in reference, ittiḥād fī al-maṣdūq) but differ conceptually or in mode of presentation. A definition that merely rephrases in different words is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنَ التَّعْرِيفِ المَذْكُورِ أُمُوراً : أَحَدُهَا : أَنَّ المُعَرِّفَ لِلمَاهِيَّةِ لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ غَيْرُهَا ؛ لأَنَّ مَعْرِفَتَهُ سَبَبُ لِمَعْرِفَتِهَا ، وَالسَّبَبُ غَيْرُ المُسَبَّبِ ، وَوَجْهُ المُغَايرَةِ فِي الحَدِّ التَّامّ : أَنَّهُ دَالٌّ عَلَى المَاهِيَّةِ تَفْصِيلاً، وَالمَحْدُودُ تُلَاحَظُ مِنْهُ المَاهِيَّةُ إِجْمَالاً ، وَاخْتِلَافُ الاِعْتِبَارِ بِالإِجْمَالِ وَالتَّفْصِيلِ كَافٍ فِي المُغَايَرَةِ. وَأَمَّا الحَدُّ النَّاقِصُ وَالرَّسْمُ مُطلَقاً، فَوَجْهُ المُغَايَرَةِ بَيْنَهُمَا وَبَيْنَ المَاهِيَّةِ وَاضِحُ، فَالتَّعْرِيفُ وَالمُعَرَّفُ مَعَ اتِّحَادِهِمَا فِي المَصْدُوقِ هُمَا مُخْتَلِفَانِ تَارَةٌ بِالمَفْهُومِ، وَتَارَةٌ بِالإِجْمَالِ وَالتَّفْصِيلِ . قوله : (لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ غَيْرُهَا مرادُهُ : أن يكون بينهما مغايرة في المعنى مِن وجةٍ مَّا مع الاتحاد في المصدوق، لا المغايرة في اللّفظ فقط ، وبه تعلم أنَّه لا تنافي بين كون الحد مغايراً للمحدود، وبين كونهما متّحدين ؛ إذ الحدُّ التَّام مثلاً هو نفس المحدود. قوله : (وَاضِحُ) بيانُهُ : أَنَّ الحدّ الناقص إنَّما يذكر فيه بعض الذاتيات، ويترك فيه ذكر البعض، والبعض مغايرٌ للكلِّ مفهوماً، وإن ساواه مصدوقاً ، والرَّسم يكونُ بالخاصَّة وحدها، أو مع الجنس، والخواص مغايرة للمختص بها مفهوماً كـ «الكاتب» مثلاً لـ «الإنسان»، فمفهومهُ يُفيد ما لا إشعار للإنسان به .
And from the aforementioned definition are derived matters: One of them: that the definiens of the essence must be other than it; because knowledge of it is a cause for knowledge of it, and the cause is other than the effect. And the aspect of difference in the complete definition is that it indicates the essence in detail, while from the defined the essence is observed in summary. And the difference of consideration by summary and detail is sufficient for difference. As for the incomplete definition and the description absolutely, the aspect of difference between them and the essence is clear. So the definition and the defined, despite their unity in reference, are different sometimes by concept and sometimes by summary and detail. His statement: 'It must be other than it' meaning: that there be between them a difference in meaning in some respect with unity in reference, not difference in wording only. And by this you know that there is no contradiction between the limit being different from the limited and them being united; for instance the complete limit is the same as the limited. His statement: 'clear' its explanation: that the incomplete limit mentions only some of the essentials and leaves out mentioning some, and the part is different from the whole in concept, even if it equals it in reference. And the description is by the property alone or with the genus, and properties are different from what they are specific to in concept, like 'writer' for example for 'human', for its concept conveys what the human does not suggest.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage explains the first condition of definition: the definiens must be other than the definiendum. The author (Bannani) begins by drawing this condition from the definition mentioned earlier. The reasoning is causal: knowledge of the definiens is the cause of knowledge of the definiendum, and the cause must be other than the effect. The author then clarifies the nature of this difference for various kinds of definition. For a complete definition (hadd tāmm), the difference lies in the mode of presentation: the definition presents the essence in detail, while the defined is observed summarily. This difference in consideration (ijmāl/tafṣīl) is sufficient for otherness. For incomplete definitions (hadd nāqiṣ) and descriptions (rasm), the difference is even more obvious, since they involve only part of the essence or external properties. The glosses further elaborate: the requisite difference is in meaning, not merely wording, and there is no contradiction between the limit being the same as the limited in reference while differing in concept. The example of 'writer' as a property of 'human' shows that the concept of 'writer' conveys something not suggested by 'human'.

Key Terms
المُعَرِّف
الحد التام
المغايرة في المعنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the aspect of difference (wajh al-mughāyara) between a complete definition (al-ḥadd al-tāmm) and the defined essence?
A) The definition is more detailed while the defined is more general in reference.
B) The definition indicates the essence in detail, while the defined is observed summarily.
C) The definition is composed of unfamiliar terms while the defined is familiar.
D) The definition is a cause while the defined is an effect.

Key Takeaway
The first condition of definition requires that the definiens be other than the definiendum in meaning, not merely in wording, and this otherness can be through detail vs. summary (for complete definition) or through part vs. whole or property vs. essence (for incomplete definitions/descriptions).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition 'al-insān is al-ḥayawān al-nāṭiq'. Explain why the definiens is other than the definiendum, identifying the aspect of otherness (tafṣīl vs. ijmāl).
?
Find a definition from a fiqh text (e.g., al-Mustasfa) and check whether the definiens is genuinely other than the definiendum according to the condition of mughāyara fī al-maʿnā. If it fails, explain why.

Resolving the Objection of Otherness in Synonym Definitions
Objection and answer on synonym definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how defining a term by a more famous synonym satisfies the condition of otherness by appealing to the property of being named.

Core Idea
Synonym definitions work because 'being named X' is a property distinct from the concept.

The condition that the definiens must be other than the definiendum seems violated when we define a term by its synonym. After all, synonyms are supposed to have the same meaning. This brief dialectical passage presents that objection and gives a crisp answer: the definiens is not the synonym's concept but the property of being named by that term. Understanding this move sharpens your ability to identify valid definitional strategies in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector argues that defining 'insān' by 'bashar' (when 'bashar' is more famous) fails because synonyms have identical meanings, so there is no difference (mughāyara) between definiendum and definiens.
The condition of otherness is fundamental in definition theory.
2
Locate the answer's logical move
The answer reinterprets the definiens as not the concept 'bashar' but the fact that the definiendum is 'what is named bashar'. This property of being named is additional to the concept itself.
The term 'property' (khāṣṣa) signals non-essential attribute.
3
Connect to definition by property
The passage classifies this as rasm bi-l-khāṣṣa (definition by property). The property 'being named bashar' is external to the essence of insān, yet it provides a valid distinguishing mark.
This is one accepted way to define, though not the highest kind.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قُلْتَ : مَا وَجْهُ المُغَايرَةِ فِي تَعْرِيفِ أَحَدِ المُتَرَادِفَيْنِ بِالآخَرِ كَتَعْرِيفِ الإِنْسَانِ بـ : «البَشَرِ إِذَا كَانَ اسْمُ البَشَرِ أَشْهَرَ مِنْهُ؟ قُلْتُ: يَأْتِي أَنَّهُ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى التَّعْرِيفِ بِالخَاصَّةِ ؛ أَي : هُوَ المُسَمَّى بِالبَشَرِ، وَكَوْنُهُ مُسَمًّى بِالبَشَرِ مُغَايرُ لِمَفْهُومِهِ .
If you say: What is the aspect of difference in defining one of the two synonyms by the other, like defining 'insān' by 'bashar' if the name 'bashar' is more famous than it? I say: It comes that it returns to definition by property; i.e., it is what is named 'bashar', and its being named 'bashar' is different from its concept.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This is a dialectical exchange: an objection and its answer. The objector points out that when we define one synonym by another—for instance, defining 'insān' as 'bashar' because 'bashar' is more well-known—there seems to be no difference in meaning between the two, since they are synonyms. So how can this satisfy the condition that the definiens must be other than the definiendum? The answer, delivered by the commentator, is that such a definition actually falls under 'definition by property' (al-taʿrīf bi-l-khāṣṣa). That is, when we say 'insān' is 'what is named bashar', the definiens is not simply the concept 'bashar' but the fact that it is named by that term. This property—being so-named—is additional to the concept itself; hence there is a genuine difference. The commentator also notes that this view is adopted by Yūsī and others, though some scholars disagree.

Key Terms
التعريف اللفظي
الخاصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the answer in this passage, defining 'insān' by 'bashar' because 'bashar' is more famous is considered what type of definition?
A) Complete definition (ḥadd tāmm)
B) Incomplete definition (ḥadd nāqiṣ)
C) Definition by property (rasm bi-l-khāṣṣa)
D) Definition by genus (jins)

Key Takeaway
Synonym definitions are valid as definitions by property, where the property of being named provides the necessary otherness.

The Second Condition: Priority of Definiens Knowledge
Author states and explains the second condition: knowledge of the definiens must precede knowledge of the definiendum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to detect whether a definition violates the second condition (priority of definiens knowledge) and identify circular definitions (dawr) in Islamic logical texts.

Core Idea
A valid definition must use terms already known; otherwise it is circular or empty.

In our previous lesson, we learned the first condition for a proper definition. Now the author of the Bannani commentary introduces the second critical condition: the definiens must be known before the definiendum. This condition ensures that the definition actually teaches something new and avoids vicious circles. We will explore the rationale, the prohibition of defining with unknowns, and the classic examples of correlatives and circular definitions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the causal rationale
The definiens is the cause of knowledge; cause must precede effect. The author argues that knowledge of the definiens is the cause of knowing the definiendum, so it must come first.
This is not temporal but logical priority.
2
Distinguish valid from invalid uses of unknown terms
Defining with an unknown term is invalid unless the unknown term is also defined. Example: defining 'human' to someone who doesn't know 'animal' requires also defining 'animal'.
This shows how the condition can be satisfied by providing definitions for both.
3
Identify circular definitions (dawr) and mutual dependents (mutadāyifān)
The passage prohibits definitions where knowledge of the definiens depends on knowledge of the definiendum. The examples of 'sun' and 'day', and 'father' and 'son' illustrate this.
Check if the definiens itself requires the definiendum to be understood.
4
Apply the condition to a real Islamic example
Consider the definition 'khamr is an intoxicating drink'. If someone does not know what 'intoxicating' means, the definition fails unless 'intoxicating' is defined. Alternatively, if 'intoxicating' were defined as 'causing loss of intellect like khamr', that would be circular.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثَّانِي: أَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ أَنْ تَكُونَ مَعْرِفَةُ المُعَرِّفِ - بِالكَسْرِ - سَابِقَةٌ عَلَى مَعْرِفَةِ المُعَرَّفِ لِوُجُوبِ تَقَدُّمِ السَّبَبِ عَلَى مُسَيَّبِهِ، وَمَعْنَاهُ : أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ أَنْ تَكُونَ أَجْزَاءُ التَّعْرِيفِ مُتَصَوَّرَةٌ عِنْدَ المُعَرِّفِ لَهُ قَبْلَ التَّعْرِيفِ بِهَا ، فَلَا يَصِحُ التَّعْرِيفُ بِمَجْهُولٍ لامْتِنَاعِ التَّوَصُّلِ بِمَجْهُولٍ إِلَى مَجْهُولٍ إِلَّا إِذَا ذُكِرَ تَعْرِيفُ المَجْهُولِ مَعَهُ ; كَأَنْ يُقَالَ فِي تَعْرِيفِ الإِنْسَانِ لِمَنْ يَجْهَلُهُ، وَيَجْهَلُ الحَيَوَانِ: «الإِنْسَانُ هُوَ الحَيَوَانُ النَّاطِقُ، وَالحَيَوَانُ هُوَ : الجِسْمُ النَّامِي : الحَسَّاسُ، وَلِهَذَا الشَّرْطِ يَمْتَنِعُ تَعْرِيفُ الشَّيْء بِمَا تَتَوَقَّفُ مَعْرِفَتُهُ عَلَى مَعْرِفَةِ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْء كَالمُتَضَايفَيْنِ كَـ: «الأُبُوَّةِ، وَالبُنُوَةِ» ; لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُعْرَفُ أَحَدُهُمَا قَبْلَ الآخَرِ، بَلْ يُعْرَفَانِ مَعاً . قوله: (سَابِقَةٌ عَلَى مَعْرِفَةِ المُعَرَّفِ) أي : لا تتوقف عليه، فلو توقفت معرفته عليه كتعريف الشَّمس» بـ: «أنَّها كوكب نهاري»، مع أنَّ النَّهار الَّذي نُسِبَ إليه متوقف تعقله على تعقل الشَّمس ; لأنَّ النَّهار الوقت من طلوع الشمس فوق الأفق إلى غروبها، لم يصح، وحينئذٍ فهذا الشَّرط يُحترز به عن أن يكون في التعريف دور، أو مجهول لم يؤت بتعريفه معه، كما أشار له هذا الشارح. قوله : (أَنْ تَكُونَ أَجْزَاءُ التَّعْرِيفِ أي الماهية نفسها، أو خواصها التي يقعُ بها التَّعريفُ.
The second: that knowledge of the definiens (with kasr) must be prior to knowledge of the definiendum, due to the necessity of the cause preceding its effect. Its meaning: that it is necessary that the parts of the definition be conceived by the one defining before defining with them. So definition by an unknown is not valid, because it is impossible to reach from an unknown to an unknown, unless the definition of the unknown is mentioned along with it; as if one says in defining 'insān' to someone who is ignorant of it and ignorant of 'ḥayawān': 'insān is the rational animal', and 'ḥayawān is the growing, sensing body'. And due to this condition, defining a thing by that whose knowledge depends on knowledge of that thing is prohibited, like the two correlatives such as 'fatherhood' and 'sonhood', because one of them is not known before the other; rather they are known together. His statement: 'prior to knowledge of the definiendum' meaning: not dependent on it. So if its knowledge were dependent on it, like defining 'sun' by 'it is a daytime star', while the day to which it is attributed is understood only by understanding the sun—because day is the time from sunrise above the horizon to sunset—it would not be valid. Hence this condition guards against there being a circle in the definition, or an unknown whose definition is not given with it, as this commentator indicated. His statement: 'the parts of the definition' meaning the essence itself, or its properties by which the definition occurs.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage presents the second condition for a valid definition: the definiens must be known prior to the definiendum. The reasoning is causal: the definiens is the cause of knowledge, so it must precede the effect. This means that the parts of the definition—whether the essential constituents (for a ḥadd) or properties (for a rasm)—must be already conceived by the learner. Defining with an unknown term is invalid, except when the unknown term is itself defined simultaneously (as when we define both 'insān' and 'ḥayawān' together). The condition also prohibits circular definitions, where knowledge of the definiendum depends on knowledge of the definiens and vice versa. Mutual dependents (mutadāyifān) like 'fatherhood' and 'sonhood' are given as examples: they cannot be defined in terms of each other because they are known together. The glosses clarify that the sun/day example is circular because 'day' is defined by the sun. Thus, this condition prevents vicious circles (dawr) and ensures the definition genuinely teaches something new.

Key Terms
الدور
المتضايفان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Defining 'human' as 'rational animal' after defining 'animal' already.
B) Defining 'sun' as 'a daytime star' when 'daytime' is defined by the presence of the sun.
C) Defining 'father' as 'parent of a son' when 'son' is already known.
D) Defining 'wine' as 'intoxicating drink' when 'intoxicating' is known.

Key Takeaway
The definiens must be known prior to the definiendum; circular definitions (dawr) violate this and teach nothing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Third Condition: Definiens Must Be Clearer than Definiendum
Author states the third condition: the definiens must be clearer (ajlā) to the hearer than the definiendum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether a given definition violates the condition that the definiens must be clearer than the definiendum.

Core Idea
A valid definition must illuminate, not merely transpose obscurity.

The third condition for a valid definition (hadd) is that the term used to define (definiens) must be clearer to the hearer than the term being defined (definiendum). This prevents defining the unknown by the equally unknown. The commentator clarifies a subtle point about the word 'ajlā' and gives an example of invalid definition: defining something by its opposite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition stated
The passage states that the definiens (al-muʿarrif) must be ajlā (clearer) than the definiendum (al-muʿarraf). Understand that this means the definiens should be more apparent and evident to the listener.
2
Understand the special usage of 'ajlā'
The commentator notes that 'ajlā' here does not mean comparative 'clearer' in the usual sense (which would imply the defined is clear already), but rather absolute 'clear'. That is, the definiens must be clear in itself.
3
Recognize the invalid case: defining by opposite
The passage gives an example: defining a thing by its opposite, such as 'the moving is what is not stationary'. This is invalid because the opposite (stationary) is equally obscure without definition.
4
Apply the condition to real definitions
When you encounter a definition, check whether the definiens uses terms that are clearer than the definiendum. If it uses an opposite or a term equally obscure, the definition fails this condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثَّالِثُ : أَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ المُعَرِّفُ - بِالكَسْرِ - أَجْلَى عِنْدَ السَّامِعِ مِنَ المُعَرَّفِ - بِالفَتْحِ - أَيْ : أَظْهَرَ مِنْهُ وَأَوْضَحَ، فَلَا يُعَرَّفُ الشَّيْءُ بِمَا يُسَاوِيهِ فِي الخَفَاءِ كَتَعْرِيفِ الزَّوْجِ ... إلخ . قوله: (أَجْلَى) هو بمعنى: «جلى»، لا على بابه مِنَ المشاركة والزّيادة؛ لاقتضائه أنَّ المحدود جلي، مع أن الجليَّ لا يُطلب تعريفه. قوله : (كَتَعْرِيفِ الزَّوْجِ» ... إلخ) هذا راجع إلى تعريف الشَّيء بضده، ومنه: «المتحرّك : ما ليس بساكن، وعكسه.
The third: that the definiens (with kasr) must be clearer (ajlā) to the hearer than the definiendum (with fatḥ), i.e., more apparent and more evident. So a thing is not defined by what equals it in obscurity, like defining 'husband'... etc. His statement: 'ajlā' means 'clear', not in its usual sense of mutual participation and increase, because it would imply that the defined is clear, while the clear does not need definition. His statement: 'like defining husband... etc.' this refers to defining a thing by its opposite, and from that: 'the moving is what is not stationary', and its converse.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage states the third condition: the definiens must be clearer (ajlā) to the hearer than the definiendum. Since the purpose of definition is to clarify, using a term that is equally obscure defeats the purpose. The gloss clarifies that 'ajlā' here means 'clear' simply, not the comparative 'clearer' in the sense of mutual participation, because that would imply the defined is already clear. The example given is defining something by its opposite, such as defining 'husband' by 'wife' (implied) or 'moving' as 'what is not stationary'. Such definitions are invalid because the opposite is equally in need of definition. This condition ensures that the definiens genuinely illuminates the definiendum.

Key Terms
أجلى
تعريف الشيء بضده

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because 'stationary' is as obscure as 'moving'.
C) Because it is a logical tautology.
D) Because 'moving' is not a genus.

Key Takeaway
The definiens must be clearer than the definiendum; defining by an opposite is invalid because it does not reduce obscurity.
